------------------ Course Code: COSC, Course Name: Computer Science ------------------

Course: COSC
Course Section: 101
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Digital Citizenship
Course Description: Provides knowledge and skills to navigate the digital society. The importance of digital participation will be investigated by studying issues surrounding digital access, skills, and utilization. Digital literacy is emphasized through the exploration of computer applications, the use of converging technologies, and online resources. This course does not assume students have any Computer Science background. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 101 or COSC 132. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 111
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Computer Programming I
Course Description: Introduction to the design, implementation, and understanding of computer programs. Topics include problem solving, algorithm design, and data and procedural abstraction, with emphasis on the development of working programs. This course should be followed by COSC 121. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 70% or higher in one of PREC 12, MATH 12, MATH 125.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 114
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Vector Graphics and Animations
Course Description: Foundation and applications of 2D /3D Euclidean geometry necessary for the computer manipulation of curves and surfaces; decomposition of a picture into basic objects; planar and spatial linear transformations; automatic picture generation and introduction to algorithmic art. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of MATH12, PREC12, or CALC12
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 121
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Computer Programming II
Course Description: Advanced programming in the application of software engineering techniques to the design and implementation of programs manipulating complex data structures. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in one of COSC 111, COSC 123.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 122
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Computer Fluency
Course Description: Introduction to computer skills (electronic communication, websites, Internet, document editing, programming, data analysis using spreadsheets/databases) and concepts (information representation, abstraction, algorithmic thinking). Course objectives are life-long productivity and understanding of technology in society. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 123
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Computer Creativity
Course Description: A hands-on introduction to programming and computer-based problem solving and creativity. Experience with application development including storytelling, graphics, games, and networking. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of COSC 111, COSC 122.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 150
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Physical Computing
Course Description: Physical computing is the design and building of hardware and software systems for sensing, processing, and affecting the analog world. Principles of physical computing, including basic electricity, digital logic, and analogue and digital electronics. Systems design for interfacing with microprocessors, sensors, and actuators using analogue and digital elements and signals. Programming for embedded systems. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite:  One of COSC 111, COSC 122, APSC 177.
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 211
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Machine Architecture
Course Description: Organization and design of computer systems and their impact on the practice of software development. Instruction set architecture and assembly programming languages, design of central processing units (CPU), memory hierarchy and cache organization, input and output programming. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 121.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 221
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Discrete Structures
Course Description: Introduction to sets, logic, combinatorics, and graph theory, as applied in computing: sets and propositions, permutations and combinations, graphs and trees, Boolean algebra, algorithms, and applications. [3-0-1]
Course Prequisite:  One of MATH 101, MATH 142, APSC 172.
Course Corequisite:  COSC 121.
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 222
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Data Structures
Course Description: Introduction to the design, implementation and analysis of data structures. Topics will include lists, stacks, queues, trees, and graphs. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 121.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 223
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Principle of Computing: Logic, Discrete Structure, and Data Structure
Course Description: Propositional logic and logic inference, problem-solving techniques (recursion, induction, and mathematical proof), models of computation (theory of finite automata), graph theory, data structures (linear data structures, dictionaries, and graphs), basic algorithmic techniques. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of COSC 114, APSC 171 and one of COSC 123, COSC 111.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 247
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Networks and Social Media
Course Description: Online social networks and digital social media. Social media platforms, channels, and software tools. Graph-theoretic and game-theoretic foundation of network analysis and network science. Network metrics and evaluation. Computational, economic, and social aspects of social media. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  COSC 223.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 264
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Web Development and Databases
Course Description: Construction of simple database-driven websites. Introduction to web programming: client-side, server-side; database design, implementation, and query. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of COSC 121, COSC 223.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 301
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Data Analytics
Course Description: Techniques for computation, analysis, and visualization of data using software. Manipulation of small and large data sets. Automation using scripting. Real-world applications from life sciences, physical sciences, economics, engineering, or psychology. No prior computing background is required. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 301, DATA 301 or DATA 501. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  Either (a) third-year standing, or (b) one of COSC 111 or COSC 122
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  DATA 301.

Course: COSC
Course Section: 303
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Numerical Analysis
Course Description: Numerical techniques for basic mathematical processes and their analysis. Taylor polynomials, root-finding, linear systems, eigenvalues, approximating derivatives, locating minimizers, approximating integrals, solving differential equations. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 303 or MATH 303. [3-1-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of MATH 200, MATH 221 and COSC 111.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  MATH 303.

Course: COSC
Course Section: 304
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Databases
Course Description: Databases from a user's perspective: querying with SQL, designing with UML, and using programs to analyze data. Construction of database-driven applications and websites and experience with current database technologies. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of COSC 111, COSC 123, APSC 177 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 305
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Project Management
Course Description: Examine tools and techniques to complete projects successfully, and within budget. Topics include Program Evaluation and Review Technique (PERT) and Critical Path Methods (CPM), and project management software. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  COSC 223 or a score of 60% or higher in COSC 121, and third-year standing
Course Corequisite:  COSC 310.
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 310
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Software Engineering
Course Description: Techniques to construct large systems using fundamental activities of specification, design, implementation, testing, and maintenance. Various life cycle models including the Unified Process. Exposure to software development tools, UML modeling techniques, good development practices, and project management. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of COSC 222, COSC 223 and, third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 315
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Operating Systems
Course Description: Introduction to batch, multiprogramming, and time-sharing systems. Process synchronization and communication. Main memory allocation techniques including virtual memory; process scheduling; deadlock avoidance and prevention; file organization and device management. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of COSC 221, COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 320
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Analysis of Algorithms
Course Description: Design and analysis of algorithms, illustrated from various problem areas. Models of computation, choice of data structures, space and time efficiency, computation complexity, algorithms for searching, sorting and graph-theoretic problems, NP-complete problems. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 320 or COSC 520. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of COSC 221, COSC 222, MATH 221.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 322
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Artificial Intelligence
Course Description: AI and intelligent agents; state space search; game playing agents; logic and knowledge-based agents; constraint programming; planning; reasoning and decision making under uncertainty; machine learning; natural language understanding. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 322 or COSC 522. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of COSC 221, COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 328
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Networks
Course Description: The five-layer Internet architecture using TCP/IP: application, transport, network, link, and physical. Topics include web protocols, network programming, routing, addressing, congestion control, error handling, Ethernet, wireless networks, security, multimedia transmission, and network management. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in all of COSC 211, COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 331
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Principles of Computer Science
Course Description: An introduction to different programming paradigms and theories of computation. Functional programming and basics of lambda calculus; logic programming and basics of propositional and first-order logic; regular languages and finite automaton. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 331 or COSC 231. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 335
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Medical Imaging and Imaging Informatics
Course Description: Fundamental image analysis techniques. Image creation, manipulation, optimization, and analysis to aid in the diagnosis and treatment of human health conditions. Generation and display of X-ray, CT, MRI, Ultrasound and Nuclear Medicine images. Imaging Informatics and its place in the Electronic Medical Record. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 335 or PHYS 336. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in PHYS 122 or (preferably) PHYS 102; and a score of 60% or higher in COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 341
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Human Computer Interaction
Course Description: Examines the basic principles behind interaction design; how humans interact with computers, as well as the user-centered design cycle; user task analysis, task models, graphical interface design, prototyping, and evaluation. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 341 or COSC 541. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  Third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 360
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Web Programming
Course Description: Design and implementation of web-based information systems and app development. Rich user interfaces, asynchronous updates, client-side and server-side scripting using standard technologies such as HTML, CSS, SVG, JavaScript, PHP. Data manipulation with SQL, JSON, XML. Modern scripting frameworks and libraries. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 121 and COSC 304 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 404
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Database System Implementation
Course Description: Fundamental concepts in constructing database systems including file organizations, storage management, system architectures, query processing/optimization, transaction management, recovery, and concurrency control. Additional topics may include distributed databases, mobile databases, and integration. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 404 or COSC 504. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 304 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 405
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Modelling and Simulation
Course Description: Numeric dynamic systems models and emphasis on discrete stochastic systems. State description of models, common model components, entities. Common simulation language. Simulation using algebraic languages. Simulation methodology: data collection, model design, output analysis, optimization, validation. Elements of queuing theory, relationship to simulation. Applications tocomputer systems models. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 405, DATA 405, COSC 505, or DATA 505. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 221 and a score of 60% or higher in COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  DATA 405.

Course: COSC
Course Section: 406
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Numerical Optimization
Course Description: Formulation and analysis of algorithms for continuous optimization problems; linear, quadratic, semi-definite, nonlinear (constrained and unconstrained), convex (smooth and non-smooth) optimization; large-scale problems; software packages and their implementation; elements of duality theory. Credit will not be granted for both COSC 406 and COSC 506. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of MATH 200, APSC 248 and one of MATH 221, APSC 179.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 407
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Parallel Computing
Course Description: Design and implementation of parallel programs including theoretical computer models, parallel architectures (distributed, multicore, GPU), and standard parallel libraries. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 407 or COSC 507. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  Either (a) COSC 111 or (b) APSC 177. Third-year standing is required.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 414
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Computer Graphics
Course Description: Human vision and colour, modelling, geometric transformations, algorithms for 2-D and 3-D graphics, hardware and system architectures, shading and lighting, animation. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of COSC 221, COSC 222 and one of MATH 221, APSC 179.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 416
Course Credits: 3-9
Course Title: Special Topics in Databases
Course Description: Advanced or specialized topics in database design, modelling, and implementation. This course may be taken more than once for credit. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 416 or COSC 516 when the subject matter is of the same nature. 
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 304 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 417
Course Credits: 3/6
Course Title: Topics in Computer Networks
Course Description: Advanced or specialized topics in emerging network technologies. With different topics, this course may be taken twice for credit. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  COSC 315 and a score of 60% or higher in COSC 328.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 419
Course Credits: 3-9
Course Title: Topics in Computer Science
Course Description: Advanced or specialized topics in computer science. Consult the department for the specific topic to be offered in any given year. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 419 or COSC 519 when the subject matter is of the same nature. 
Course Prequisite:  Fourth-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 420
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Algorithms and Intelligent Systems for Bioinformatics
Course Description: Algorithmic techniques for problems in bioinformatics. Analysis and comparison of genetic sequences; construction of phylogenetic trees; prediction of biomolecular structures; construction and analysis of biopolymer interaction networks; pattern discovery in biological data; techniques from artificial intelligence. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  COSC 222 and one of COSC 320, COSC 322.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 421
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Network Science
Course Description: Graphs and complex networks in scientific research. Probabilistic and statistical models. Structures, patterns, and behaviors in networks. Algorithmic and statistical methods (online/mobile), social networks, and social media platforms. Social influence, information diffusion, and viral marketing. Sentiment analysis and opinion mining. Data privacy. Search engines and recommendation systems. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 421, DATA 421 or DATA 521. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  Third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  DATA 421.

Course: COSC
Course Section: 435
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Computer-Based Image Analysis
Course Description: Digital processing of remotely sensed image data. Techniques for acquiring, calibrating, registering, enhancing, and interpreting digital images are included. [2-0-2]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 442
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Mobile Educational Game Development
Course Description: Game design and development on a mobile platform with special attention to educational games. Topics may include: educational frameworks, storytelling techniques, game design, iterative prototyping, evaluation methodology, learner modeling, and learning analytics. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 442 or COSC 542. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of COSC 341, COSC 310.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 445
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Computer Vision
Course Description: Processing and interpretation of images: image sensing, filtering, algorithms for colour analysis, texture description, image segmentation, and object recognition. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  COSC 222 and one of MATH 200, APSC 248 and one of MATH 221, APSC 179.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 447
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Directed Studies in Software Maintenance
Course Description: Maintenance of a large software system including prioritizing requests, modifying the design, implementing new features, fixing bugs, and regression testing. The student will undertake the maintenance of an existing project. 
Course Prequisite:  Third-year standing and permission of the department head.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 448
Course Credits: 3/6
Course Title: Directed Studies in Computer Science
Course Description: Supervised reading, participation in a seminar, and one or more programming projects. With different topics, this course may be taken twice for credit. 
Course Prequisite:  Third-year standing and permission of the department head.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: COSC
Course Section: 449
Course Credits: 6
Course Title: Honours Thesis
Course Description: Students will undertake a research project as agreed upon by the student, supervising faculty member, and department head. A written thesis and a public presentation (poster or seminar) are required. 
Course Prequisite:  Fourth-year standing; admission to the B.A. or B.Sc. Computer Science Honours Program; and permission of the department head.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Section: 110
Course Credits: 6
Course Title: Co-operative Work Placement I
Course Description: Supervised, technical work experience in an established company or organization for a minimum of three months. Technical report required. Restricted to students meeting the requirements of the Faculty of Applied Science and the Co-operative Education program.

Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: APSC
Course Section: 169
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Fundamentals of Sustainable Engineering Design
Course Description: Theory and practice of sustainable engineering. Awareness and risk analysis of potential impacts on society and the environment over the lifecycle of engineering projects. Engineering design process, project lifecycle, and professional responsibility. Team-based design project. [3-2*-2*]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: APSC
Course Section: 171
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Engineering Drawing and CAD/CAM

Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Section: 172
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Engineering Analysis I
Course Description: Functions, limits, differentiation, applications of derivatives, integration, applications of definite integrals. [3-0-1]

Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3

Course Equivalency: None

Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Engineering Computation and Instrumentation

Course Equivalency: None

Course: APSC
Course Section: 178
Course Credits: 4
Course Title: Electricity, Magnetism, and Waves
Course Description: Coulomb's law, electric field, Gauss' law, electric potential, conductors, capacitance, electric currents, resistance, DC circuits, magnetic fields and forces, sources of magnetic fields, electromagnetic induction, mechanical waves, electromagnetic waves, light propagation, geometrical optics. [4-0-2]
Course Prequisite:  APSC 172.

Course: APSC
Course Section: 179
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Linear Algebra for Engineers

Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: APSC
Course Section: 180
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Statics
Course Description: Force vectors, Cartesian coordinate system, free body diagram, dot and cross products, forces equilibrium of particles, force and moment equilibrium of rigid bodies, analysis of trusses, frames and machines, friction, wedges, pulleys, and belts. Applications of linear algebra in statics. [3-0-2]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite:  APSC 179.
Course Equivalency: None

Course: APSC
Course Section: 181
Course Credits: 3

Course Section: 111
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Sociology I
Course Description: Studies how society influences human behaviour. How is society organized and structured? How does it affect the way we think and act? What is the relationship between individuals and society? What is our social nature? Why is there inequality in the world? [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: SOCI
Course Section: 121
Course Credits: 3

Course Prequisite:  SOCI 111.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: SOCI

Course Credits: 3

Course Title: Introduction to Income Taxes in Canada
Course Description: Introduction to the Income Tax Act (Canada). Focuses on fundamental tax principles as well as developing familiarity in using the Income Tax Act and other tax research tools. Topics include sources of income, computing income for tax purposes for individuals and corporations, tax planning opportunities, and other tax issues. Credit will be granted for only one of MGMT 402 or MGMT 432. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  Fourth-year standing in the B.Mgt. program or Faculty of Management permission.
Course Corequisite:  All of MGMT 400, MGMT 403.

Course Section: 435
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Risk Management
Course Description: Introduction to the financial instruments, methods, and tools used in financial risk management. Methodology applies to both corporate and investment settings for managing exchange rate risk, interest rate risk, market risk, and credit risk. Focuses on three types of derivative securities: forwards and futures, options, and swaps. Understanding of the basic properties of these instruments, their hedging uses, and their valuation principles. Value-at-risk and options theory will also be covered. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  Fourth-year standing in the B.Mgt. program or Faculty of Management permission.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: MGMT
Course Section: 436
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Investments
Course Description: Basic principles and tools of investment analysis. Understanding of the properties and uses of three broad types of financial securities: equity securities (common stock), fixed income securities (government and corporate bonds), and derivative securities (e.g., futures, options). The trading process, portfolio theory (risk-return and risk-arbitrage models), security analysis, and investment performance evaluation. [3-0-0]

Course Title: Environmental Science
Course Description: A quantitative and scientific approach to the understanding of global energy, water and nutrient cycling; growth of human populations and their effects on the environment and ecosystem function. Functional understanding of modern environmental issues, and the requirements of, and opportunities for, sustainability. Credit will be granted for only one of EESC 101, SUST 100, GEOG 213. [3-0-0]

Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Earth Science
Course Description: Origin, structure and composition of Earth. Plate tectonics as the unifying mechanism for mountain building, formation of ocean basins, and assembly and break-up of continents. Minerals, rocks, Earth surface processes, geological maps, natural resources and hazards. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Earth History

Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Optical Mineralogy and Petrology

Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Hydrology

Course Section: 212
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Atmospheric Environments

Course Section: 213
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introductory Forest Science and Management
Course Description: Global forests, classification, silviculture, forest tenure systems, forest policy evolution, forest regulations, and the profession. Overview of forest disturbance impacts, eco-forestry, sustainable forest management, eco-certification, the role of information technologies and research. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of EESC 111, GEOG 108.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: EESC
Course Section: 222
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Geomorphology
Course Description: Landform assemblages and processes of landscape evolution on Earth. Fundamental concepts, including system equilibrium, thresholds, complex response to external forces, and scale dependency, with application to mountains, rivers, coasts, and glaciated terrain. Laboratory exercises require field work in lab time. Required one-day, weekend trip. Credit will be granted for only one of EESC 222 or GEOG 222. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  Either (a) GEOG 108 and GEOG 109; or (b) MATH 100 and EESC 111 or (c) MATH 100 and 6 credits of first-year lab science.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  GEOG 222.

Course: EESC
Course Section: 301
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Limnology
Course Description: Integrated approaches to freshwater science and its place in environmental science. Ecosystem ecology of inland waters relating to aquatic organisms with their physical and chemical environment. Participation in a one-day weekend field trip in September or early October is required. Credit will be granted for only one of EESC 301 or BIOL 307. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of BIOL 116, BIOL 125. Third-year standing in Freshwater Science, Earth and Environmental Sciences, or Environmental Chemistry. One of BIOL 201, BIOL 203 or BIOL 375 is recommended.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  BIOL 307.

Course: EESC
Course Section: 303
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Oceanography
Course Description: Geological, chemical, physical and biological oceanography using a multidisciplinary approach. Origins of oceans, plate tectonics and ocean basins, marine sediments, physical properties and composition of seawater, ocean-atmosphere interactions, surface and deep currents, waves, tides, primary productivity, pelagic and benthic ecosystems, methods of ocean investigation. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  Either (a) two of EESC 101, EESC 111, EESC 121, GEOG 108, GEOG 109 or (b) one of EESC 301, BIOL 307, CHEM 301, EESC 309. Third-year standing.

Course Section: 305
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Land-Use Hydrology
Course Description: Interaction between vegetation and water. Effects of land use on the hydrology of watersheds. A range of topical aspects of land-use hydrology. Specific practices such as the hydrological effects of clearfelling, regrowth of forest (tree planting), grazing, cultivation, irrigation, and wildland fire. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  Third-year standing.
Course Corequisite:  One of EESC 205, GEOG 205.

Course Title: Global Biogeochemistry

Course Prequisite:  Either (a) EESC 101 and EESC 111; or (b) GEOG 108 and GEOG 109; or (c) one of BIOL 201, BIOL 203 or (d) one of CHEM 301, CHEM 302.

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: History of Economic Thought

The Greek, Islamic, and Medieval scholars; the Physiocrats, Adam Smith, Malthus, Bentham, Ricardo, Mill, Marx, Keynes, and other major economic thinkers. Development of fundamental economic ideas and conflicting perspectives are studied within their social and economic context. [3-0-0]

Course Prequisite:  All of MATH 221, MATH 311.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Biophysics
Course Description: Analysis of biological systems from a physicist's perspective. Introduction to physics underlying biological phenomena, and range of applicability of simple physical principles. Form and size in animals, strength and energy storage in structural elements, thermal regulation, fluid motion within organisms, life in fluids, and molecular physics topics. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  MATH 101 and either (a) PHYS 102 or (b) a score of 68% or higher in PHYS 112 and a score of 68% or higher in PHYS 122. Third-year standing in Science or a 200-level PHYS course taken concurrently.

Course Equivalency: None

Course Title: Waves

[3-0-0]

[3-0-0]

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Radiation Dosimetry
Course Description: The fundamentals of radiation dosimetry, ionization cavity theories, and radiation dosimetry protocols. A variety of absolute and relative dosimetry techniques are also covered, with hands-on experience provided through a series of lab exercises on medical linear accelerators. Monte Carlo simulation of radiation transport for dosimetry applications is introduced.

Course Title: Introduction to Physical Chemistry
Course Description: Principles of chemical kinetics, reaction mechanisms, and chemical thermodynamics. Credit will be granted for only one of CHEM 201 or 210. [3-3-1*]
Course Prequisite:  MATH 101 and one of PHYS 102, PHYS 122 and one of CHEM 113, CHEM 123. A minimum grade of 65% in CHEM 113 is strongly recommended. MATH 200 is also strongly recommended.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 203
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Organic Chemistry
Course Description: Structure, bonding, and physical properties of aliphatic and aromatic compounds; conformational analysis, stereochemistry, and NMR spectroscopy; substitution and elimination reactions of alkyl halides; ethers, epoxides, aldehydes, ketones. Credit will not be granted for only one of CHEM 203 or CHEM 213. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 113, CHEM 123. A minimum grade of 65% in CHEM 113 is strongly recommended. For Chemistry, Biochemistry, and Environmental Chemistry majors. Other students should enrol in CHEM 213.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 204
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Organic Chemistry
Course Description: Mechanistic analysis of chemical reactivity of common functional groups, with focus on carbonyl chemistry; aromaticity and aromatic substitution; functional group transformations in organic synthesis; carbohydrates, amino acids, proteins, heterocycles. Credit will be granted for only one of CHEM 204 or CHEM 214. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  CHEM 203. For Chemistry, Biochemistry, and Environmental Chemistry majors. Other students should enrol in CHEM 214.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 210
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Physical Chemistry for Earth, Environmental, and Life Sciences
Course Description: Intended for students in earth, environmental, and life sciences. Thermodynamics and kinetics as they apply to natural systems. This course cannot be used for credit by Chemistry Majors. Credit will be granted for only one of CHEM 201 or 210. [3-3-1*]
Course Prequisite:  MATH 101 and one of PHYS 102, PHYS 122 and one of CHEM 113, CHEM 123. A minimum grade of 65% in CHEM 113 is strongly recommended.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 211
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Analytical Chemistry
Course Description: Statistical analysis and errors of measurement, method development and validation, solution equilibria as applied to analysis, analysis of acids and bases, analytical electrochemistry, chemical separation, introduction to gas and liquid chromatography. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 113, CHEM 123 and one of PHYS 102, PHYS 122.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 213
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Organic Chemistry for Biological Sciences I
Course Description: Structure, bonding, and physical properties of organic compounds; conformational analysis, stereochemistry, and chirality; reactions of alkenes, alkyl halides, and alcohols. Emphasis will be placed on biological applications. Credit will be granted for only one of CHEM 203 or CHEM 213. [3-3*-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 113, CHEM 123. Not for Chemistry, Biochemistry, or Environmental Chemistry majors. Such students should enrol in CHEM 203.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 214
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Organic Chemistry for Biological Sciences II
Course Description: Mechanistic description of aromatic substitution, reactions of carbonyl compounds and amines, oxidation/reduction reactions. Chemistry of carbohydrates, amino acids, vitamins, lipids, nucleotides. Chemical principles of biological catalysis and metabolism. Credit will be granted for only one of CHEM 204 or CHEM 214. [3-3*-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 203, CHEM 213. Not for Chemistry, Biochemistry, or Environmental Chemistry majors. Such students should enrol in CHEM 204.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 220
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Atomic Structure and Molecular Bonding
Course Description: Examination of various theories of atomic structure and molecular bonding, and their use to explain chemical and physical properties of atoms and molecules. Atomic wave mechanics, Lewis theory, valence bond theory, crystal field theory, symmetry and group theory, and molecular orbital theory of diatomic and polyatomic molecules and extended solids. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 113, CHEM 123. A minimum grade of 65% in CHEM 113 is strongly recommended.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: CHEM

Course Equivalency: None

Course Title: Methods in Forensic Chemical Analysis
Course Description: Concepts in the forensic chemical analysis of materials. Course Title: Bioinorganic Chemistry

[3-4*-0]

Course Title: Coordination Chemistry
Course Description: Analysis of the coordination chemistry of <i>d</i>- and <i>f</i>-block metals including structure, bonding descriptions, spectroscopic and magnetic properties, and kinetics and mechanism of substitution and redox reactions. [3-4*-0]

Course: CHEM
Course Section: 338
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Organometallic Chemistry
Course Description: Examination of the structure, bonding, reactivity, and catalysis of organometallic compounds of the <i>d-</i>block metals. A survey of ligands unique to organometallic chemistry is followed by an examination of the mechanisms of common reactions and important catalytic cycles. [3-4*-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: </i> CHEM 220 and one of CHEM 204, CHEM 214.

Course Section: 403
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Enzymology
Course Description: Enzyme kinetics: steady-state kinetic analyses, fast-reaction methods, kinetic isotope effects. Catalytic mechanisms: coenzymology, radical-mediated reactions, catalytic rate enhancements. Special topics: enzyme evolution, multifunctional enzymes, biocatalysis, protein engineering. Credit will be granted for only one of CHEM 403, BIOC 403, CHEM 413 or CHEM 569. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of BIOC 304, BIOL 311.

Course Equivalency:  BIOC 403.

------------------ Course Code: DATA, Course Name: Data Science ------------------

Course: DATA
Course Section: 301
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Data Analytics
Course Description: Techniques for computation, analysis, and visualization of data using software. Manipulation of small and large data sets. Automation using scripting. Real-world applications from life sciences, physical sciences, economics, engineering, or psychology. No prior computing background is required. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 301, DATA 301 or DATA 501. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  Either (a) third-year standing, or (b) one of COSC 111 or COSC 122
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  COSC 301.

Course: DATA
Course Section: 311
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Machine Learning
Course Description: Regression, classification, resampling, model selection and validation, fundamental properties of matrices, dimension reduction, tree-based methods, unsupervised learning. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  both of (one of STAT 230 or 75% in either APSC 254, BIOL 202, or PSYO 373) and (one of COSC 111 or APSC 177).
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: DATA
Course Section: 405
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Modelling and Simulation
Course Description: Numeric dynamic systems models and emphasis on discrete stochastic systems. State description of models, common model components, entities. Common simulation language. Simulation using algebraic languages. Simulation methodology: data collection, model design, output analysis, optimization, validation. Elements of queuing theory, relationship to simulation. Applications tocomputer systems models. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 405, DATA 405, COSC 505, or DATA 505. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  A score of 60% or higher in COSC 221 and a score of 60% or higher in COSC 222.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  COSC 405.

Course: DATA
Course Section: 407
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Sampling and Design
Course Description: Planning and practice of data collection. Pros and cons of both observational and experimental data. Survey samples: random sampling; bias and variance; unequal probability sampling; systematic, multistage, and stratified sampling; ratio and regression estimators. Experimental design: simple one-way comparisons; designs with randomization restrictions including blocking, split-plots, nested and repeated measures designs. Credit will be granted for only one of DATA 407 or STAT 507. [3-1-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of STAT 230, PSYO 372, BIOL 202, ECON 327.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: DATA
Course Section: 410
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Regression and Generalized Linear Models
Course Description: Regression, linear models, generalized linear models, additive models, generalized additive models, mixed models. Theory and numerical performance. Credit will be granted for only one of DATA 410 or STAT 538. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  DATA 311.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: DATA
Course Section: 419
Course Credits: 3-9

Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

(online/mobile) social networks and social media platforms. Social influence, information diffusion, and viral marketing. Sentiment analysis and opinion mining. Data privacy. Search engines and recommendation systems. Credit will be granted for only one of COSC 421, DATA 421 or DATA 521. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite:  Third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  COSC 421.

------------------ Course Code: BIOC, Course Name: Biochemistry ------------------

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 304
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Molecular Biochemistry I
Course Description: Principles of thermodynamics and reaction kinetics in biochemistry. Acid/base biochemistry. Structure and function of lipids, amino acids, proteins, carbohydrates, nucleotides, and nucleic acids. Enzyme kinetics. Credit will only be granted for one of BIOC 304 or BIOL 311. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 204, CHEM 214.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 305
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Molecular Biochemistry II
Course Description: Metabolic pathways with a mechanistic perspective including regulation and control of carbohydrate, lipid, amino acid, and nucleotide catabolism and anabolism. Oxidative- and photo-phosphorylation. The biochemistry and molecular biology of signal transduction, replication, DNA repair, transcription, translation, and gene regulation. Credit will only be granted for one of BIOC 305 or BIOL 319. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of BIOC 304, BIOL 200.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 307
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Enology I
Course Description: Chemistry and biochemistry of winemaking (enology) and grape-growing (viticulture) including development of the important major constituents of a wine; ethanol, acids, sugars, and colour; the subtle aspects of the aroma; odour-active compounds and how they form; and the effects of storing a wine in oak barrels. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 204, CHEM 214.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 308
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Pharmacology I
Course Description: Principles of pharmacology, including pharmacokinetics and pharmacodynamics of drug action, pharmacology associated with the autonomic nervous system (sympathetic and parasympathetic branches), the neuromuscular junction, the inflammatory response, chronic obstructive pulmonary diseases, peptic ulcers, and general and local anaesthesia. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOL 200 and one of CHEM 204, CHEM 214.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 309
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Pharmacology II
Course Description: Continuation of Pharmacology I. Expands on topics including pharmacokinetics and pharmacodynamics of drug action, interaction of drugs with the autonomic nervous system (ANS), the inflammatory response, and the treatment of chronic diseases. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOC 308.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 310
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Plant Chemistry
Course Description: Chemical constituents of plants, their synthesis, their contribution to key metabolic processes, and the regulation of their biosynthesis. Synthesis of alkaloids, secondary metabolites, nutrients, and bioactive compounds. Discovery of new phytochemicals and human uses of plants. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of CHEM 204, CHEM 214 and one of BIOL 200, BIOL 210, BIOL 319, BIOC 305.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 393
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Biochemistry Laboratory
Course Description: Topics include protein separation, enzyme kinetics, ELISA, DNA Ligation and Transformation, PCR, RFLP analysis, Agarose gel electrophoresis, STR and VNTR analysis, and gene regulation. Credit will be granted for only one of BIOC 393 or BIOL 393. [0-4-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOC 304 and one of BIOL 200, BIOL 228, CHEM 204, CHEM 214.
Course Corequisite:  BIOL 366.
Course Equivalency:  BIOL 393.

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 402
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Proteins: Structure and Function
Course Description: Structural components of proteins; classification by primary, secondary, and tertiary structure; protein chemistry and purification; peptide and protein synthesis by chemical means; and three-dimensional structure determination using X-ray diffraction and NMR. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of BIOC 304, BIOL 311.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 403
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Enzymology
Course Description: Enzyme kinetics: steady-state kinetic analyses, fast-reaction methods, kinetic isotope effects. Catalytic mechanisms: coenzymology, radical-mediated reactions, catalytic rate enhancements. Special topics: enzyme evolution, multifunctional enzymes, biocatalysis, protein engineering. Credit will be granted for only one of BIOC 403, CHEM 403, CHEM 413, CHEM 569. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of BIOC 304, BIOL 311.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  CHEM 403.

Course: BIOC
Course Section: 405
Course Credits: 3

Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOC

Course: FREN
Course Section: 460
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: 17th-Century French Tragedy
Course Description: French classical tragedies through works of Corneille and Racine. Aesthetic and political forces that helped shape these plays will be examined as well as the relationship between theatre and political power. Works will be studied in their socio-historical context and using current literary criticism. This course takes an interdisciplinary approach, incorporating European visual representations of Baroque and Classical aesthetics to assist with comprehension and analysis of texts. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  FREN 353 and one of FREN 330, FREN 360, FREN 362.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: FREN
Course Section: 461
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: 17th- and 18th-Century French Comedy
Course Description: Explores French comedies through a selection of works by authors such as Moli?re, Lesage, Marivaux, and Beaumarchais. Examines the aesthetic and political forces that shaped these plays, as well as the relationships between comedy and the representation of class and gender. Plays will be studied in their socio-historical context and approached using current literary criticism. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  FREN 353 and one of FREN 330, FREN 360, FREN 362.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Competition, predation, and an exploration of processes that promote species coexistence and lead to the maintenance of species diversity. Course Title: Immunology

Immune system, innate immunity and complement, adaptive immunity, cellular and humoral immune response, cytokines, T-cell activation, the major histocompatibility complex, antibody structure and genetics, immune system and cancer, AIDS, autoimmunity, hypersensitivity. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOL 228.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 319
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Biochemistry II
Course Description: Continuation of BIOL 311. Energy production via glycolysis, oxidative phosphorylation, and photosynthesis. Integration and control of carbohydrate, lipid, and protein metabolism. Synthesis, and metabolism of nucleic acids and the biochemistry of gene function. Credit will only be granted for one of BIOL 319 or BIOC 305. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOL 311.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 330
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Freshwater Microbiology
Course Description: Integrates taxonomy, physiology, and ecosystem functioning of freshwater microbes. Effects of microbial activities in perturbed aquatic environments will be examined. Labs introduce basic and advanced techniques for identification, enumeration, and measuring biogeochemical activity within an aquatic and experimental context. Note: this course will be offered on alternate years. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  Either (a) one of BIOL 307, EESC 301 or (b) one of BIOL 209, BIOL 210, BIOL 275 and one of BIOL 204, BIOL 205.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 341
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Neurobiology
Course Description: The nervous system control of animal behavior. Examples include: sensory processing and communication, predator-prey interactions, migration, motor-coordination, daily and seasonal changes in activity, cellular mechanisms of learning and memory. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOL 200.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 350
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Clinical Neuroscience
Course Description: The structural, biochemical, and functional changes that characterize clinically-important diseases of the nervous system, including: brain and spinal cord trauma; developmental disorders, memory, and memory dysfunction; neurodegenerative diseases; mood and anxiety disorders; epilepsy; and maintenance of homeostasis. [3-0-0]

Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 354
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Cell Physiology
Course Description: The cell is the fundamental unit of life. This course delineates a number of shared biological processes conducted at the cellular level and similar across a wide range of organisms (e.g., acquisition of usable energy, energy storage, transport processes, irritability, and contractability). [3-3*-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOL 200 and one of BIOL 202, STAT 230 and one of PHYS 102, PHYS 122.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 356
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Comparative Animal Physiology
Course Description: Comparative course concerning the evolution and advantage of systems design in a variety of animals. Two underlying themes include the principles of homeostasis - the regulation of a constant internal state - and the systems involved in maintaining a constant internal environment: cardiovascular, respiratory, osmoregulatory, and endocrine. [3-3*-0]
Course Prequisite:  BIOL 354.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 357
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Entomology
Course Description: General survey of the evolution, classification, and biology of insects, with a special emphasis on their functional ecology. Experiments using insect systems as well as master techniques for collecting and curating insect specimens will be conducted in the lab. A properly-curated collection is a requirement for this course. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of BIOL 201, BIOL 203. BIOL 205 is recommended.

Course Equivalency: None

Course: BIOL
Course Section: 358
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Plant Ecophysiology

Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Developmental Biology
Course Description: Principles of animal development. Embryonic development of key invertebrates is compared to vertebrates at the morphological, genetic, and epigenetic levels. Differential gene expression and cell signaling responsible for the specification of embryonic cell fates and pattern formation will be compared in various animals. Credit will be granted for only one of BIOL 363 or BIOL 263. [3-3-0]

Course Equivalency: None

------------------ Course Code: ANTH, Course Name: Anthropology ------------------

Course: ANTH
Course Section: 100
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Cultural Anthropology
Course Description: An overview of social and cultural anthropology - its origins, its distinctive methods and concepts, and its place in the contemporary world. A critical examination of human diversity and how social and cultural differences are produced and shaped by local and global patterns. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: ANTH
Course Section: 103
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to World Archaeology
Course Description: Peoples and cultures of prehistory. Examines archaeologists and their work in archaeological sites around the world, from the earliest evidence of humankind and hunting and gathering culture, to the emergence of civilization and state-level societies. Credit will be granted for only one of ANTH 103 and either ANTH 104 or ANTH 251. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: ANTH
Course Section: 111
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Biological Anthropology

Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: ANTH

Course Equivalency: None

Course Section: 302
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Governance
Course Description: Critically examines various traditional Indigenous governance models and the Indigenous response to European attempts to establish political control. Issues such as land ownership, sovereignty, justice, treaty making, and the roles of women in Indigenous governance will be explored. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  INDG 100. 3 additional credits of INDG courses at the 200-level; and third-year standing.

Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 303
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Studies Theory and Methodology
Course Description: Conceptualizations from an Indigenous perspective are central to this course. Includes an analysis of current conceptual paradigms within the social sciences, humanities, and performing arts, with a consideration of their appropriateness and applicability for Indigenous studies. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  INDG 100 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 304
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Studies Field Methods
Course Description: Research strategies and research techniques used in Indigenous studies and related disciplines. These elements will be applied to various topical issues including intellectual property rights, research ethics, oral histories, ethnographic research, and the use of statistics (both descriptive and inferential). [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  INDG 100 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 305
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Justice
Course Description: Decolonial Indigenous concepts, principles and historical consciousness of justice and anti-violence praxis in community-and-land based contexts. Locating agency with Indigenous peoples and Indigenous justice practices, the course puts primacy on ways that Indigenous peoples have engaged in and continue to enact justice. Revitalization of Indigenous knowledge informs ethical and moral issues addressed in relation to healing, and collective transformation. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  INDG 100 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 306
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Land Rights
Course Description: Legal theories under British Law or its historical derivations that have been used to justify the colonization of Indigenous peoples. Legal arguments and anthropological evidence raised by Indigenous groups to challenge those theories. Particular reference is paid to Canada, Australia, New Zealand, and the United States. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  INDG 100 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 307
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Traditional Ecological Knowledge
Course Description: Shows how human life depends on complex systems of cultural knowledge about the natural world. Indigenous people's biological classification and nomenclatural systems, ethnobiology, and Indigenous explanatory models of environmental systems and the application of this knowledge in practice. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  INDG 100 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 308
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Culture, Heritage, and Intellectual Property
Course Description: Indigenous Peoples' cultural heritage in the Americas and other continents. Many manifestations of Indigenous cultures will be discussed, as well as the many complex issues that have arisen regarding Indigenous heritage in the colonial and neo-colonial periods such as, customary laws, misappropriation, misrepresentation, repatriation, and legal protection and regulation. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  INDG 100 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 309
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Perspectives on Health
Course Description: Introduction to current thinking about Indigenous peoples' health, and especially Indigenous peoples' perspectives on health and contemporary health systems. Includes a critical examination of concepts of health within the context of ongoing processes of colonization. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  Third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: INDG
Course Section: 310
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Indigenous Women's Perspectives: Gender, Nation, State, Resistance
Course Description: Historical realities of the salience of states and nations in the lives of Indigenous women. Indigenous methods, de-colonial historical analysis, and gender theory are used to analyze Indigenous women's and peoples' resistances to invasion, colonization, occupation, settler states, and dispossession. Course Equivalency: None

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 422
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Fluvial Geomorphology
Course Description: Geomorphic forms and processes within and along streams and rivers; flow hydraulics; sediment transport and bedform mechanics; hydraulic geometry; channel and floodplain dynamics; sediment yield; river habitat and stream rehabilitation. Credit will be granted for only one of GEOG 422 or EESC 422. [3-0-1]
Course Prequisite:  One of EESC 222, GEOG 222, APSC 253.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  EESC 422.

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 423
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Development of Environmental Thought
Course Description: An examination of attitudes that have influenced land use and environmental change in the past and present. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of GEOG 128, GEOG 129 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 425
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Feminist Geographies of (Un)Belonging
Course Description: Transnational and decolonizing feminist approaches to the geography of power as manifested through contemporary political identities. Focus on relationships between state-mediated categories of (un)belonging such as 'citizen', 'migrant', 'refugee', 'aboriginal', and 'illegal'. Emphasis on borders, border-identities, and multicultural/settler societies such as Australia, Israel, Canada and the United States. Credit will be granted for only one of GEOG 425 or GWST 425. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of GEOG 358, GWST 110, and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  GWST 425.

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 427
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: NeoGeography
Course Description: Explores the development of NeoGeography and the geoweb: its relationship to geographic theories and concepts; its changing role in influencing the way in which we understand our relationship to space, place and the world around us. [2-0-1]
Course Prequisite:  All of GEOG 128, GEOG 129 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 429
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Sexuality and Space
Course Description: Interdisciplinary examination of the relationships between gender, sexuality, space, and place. Focus on social investments in race, sexuality, gender, (dis)ability, and citizenship as spatial technologies of belonging and power. Emphasis on queer and critical gender studies approaches to the subfield of cultural geography. Credit will be granted for only one of GWST 429 or GEOG 429. [0-0-3]
Course Prequisite:  One of GWST 223, GWST 216, GEOG 358 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  GWST 429.

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 431
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Resource Management Policy and Practice
Course Description: Contemporary issues in resource and environmental management including decision-making theory and real-world processes at the policy and field levels. Case studies illustrate stakeholder behaviours from conflict to co-operation. Focus on the Okanagan. [1-0-2]
Course Prequisite:  One of GEOG 128, GEOG 129, GEOG 310 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 434
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Geography of Tourism Development
Course Description: Implications, character, and problems of existing and potential tourism resources. Concepts of tourism supply, demand, and impacts are considered and applied to the Okanagan Valley. Nature and significance of tourism; tourism resources; demands for tourism; economic, environmental, social, and cultural impacts of tourism. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of GEOG 128, GEOG 129 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 435
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Wine Geographies
Course Description: Geographical expressions and processes of wine, viniculture, and viticulture. Appellation and terroir frame investigation of the nature-human interface in wine production and consumption. Geographic approaches include cultural history, global and localized political economies, cultural adaptation to climate, and physical geography. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of GEOG 108, GEOG 109, GEOG 128, GEOG 129 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 436
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Coastal Geomorphology
Course Description: Geomorphic forms and processes along coasts; waves and currents; sediment transport mechanics; beach and nearshore morphodynamics; aeolian forms and processes. May include one or more required one-day weekend field trips. Credit will be granted for only one of GEOG 436 or EESC 436. [3-3-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of EESC 222, GEOG 222, APSC 253.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  EESC 436.

Course: GEOG
Course Section: 437
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Terrain Analysis
Course Description: Identification, mapping, and quantification of terrain morphologies in the field and from remote sensing following professional codes of practice. Twelve days of field instruction over a two week period following spring exams. Students must arrange own transportation to/from field locations. Credit will be granted for only one of GEOG 437 or EESC 437. 
Course Prequisite:  One of EESC 222, GEOG 222, GEOG 317, ENGR 340. Third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  EESC 437.

Course Section: 451
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Urban Planning
Course Description: Urban and regional planning issues from a geographical perspective. [3-0-0]

Course Title: Cartography and Society

Emphasis on processes of research-based writing. [3-0-0]

Course Title: Hebrew Scriptures: Biblical Backgrounds to English Literature
Course Description: Survey course to acquaint students with texts of the Hebrew Scriptures (the Old Testament) which have influenced Western literature. Students will study these texts as literary texts, paying particular attention to contexts in which they were composed and the different ways they have been read. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  Two of ENGL 112, ENGL 114, ENGL 150, ENGL 151, ENGL 153 or 6 credits of 100-level English. ENGL 112 and ENGL 114 may not both be taken for credit.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: ENGL
Course Section: 243
Course Credits: 3

Course Title: Foundations: Interdisciplinary Theory and Method in Literary Research

Course: ENGL
Course Section: 270
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Topics in Women's Literature
Course Description: Exploration of ways in which women have been represented in and have contributed to the literary tradition by examining women's writing in a particular historical, national, and/or regional context (e.g., the English renaissance), on particular topics (e.g., war, religion, or work), or from a specific race or class (e.g., black women's writing). Students can elect to transfer this course as English or Women's Studies credit for this course. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  Two of ENGL 112, ENGL 114, ENGL 150, ENGL 151, ENGL 153 or 6 credits of 100-level English. ENGL 112 and ENGL 114 may not both be taken for credit.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: ENGL
Course Section: 294
Course Credits: 3/6
Course Title: Interdisciplinary Perspectives in English Literature
Course Description: Addresses the interdisciplinary perspectives that have fashioned the creation and study of English literature, specifically the ways in which English literature as a discipline has been shaped through its interaction with a wide variety of discourses from areas such as medicine, science, psychology and the visual arts. This course may involve cross-discipline pedagogies, cross-cultural approaches, experiential learning, and / or undergraduate research opportunities. 3-0-0
Course Prequisite:  Two of ENGL 112, ENGL 114, ENGL 150, ENGL 151, ENGL 153 or 6 credits of 100-level English. ENGL 112 and ENGL 114 may not both be taken for credit.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Section: 297
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Reading Animals
Course Description: Representations of animals in contemporary culture, including philosophical ethics, critical animal studies theory, and analysis of text and image. Explores novels, graphic novels, poems, plays and films that attempt to investigate and question the boundary we imagine to exist between ourselves and other animals. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  6 credits of 100-level English.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Prequisite:  One of GWST 216, GWST 223, and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: GWST
Course Section: 425
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Feminist Geographies of (Un)Belonging
Course Description: Transnational and decolonizing feminist approaches to the geography of power as manifested through contemporary political identities. Focus on relationships between state-mediated categories of (un)belonging such as 'citizen', 'migrant', 'refugee', 'aboriginal', and 'illegal'. Emphasis on borders, border-identities, and multicultural/settler societies such as Australia, Israel, Canada and the United States. Credit will be granted for only one of GWST 425 or GEOG 425. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of GEOG 358, GWST 110, and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  GEOG 425.

Course: GWST
Course Section: 429
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Sexuality and Space
Course Description: Interdisciplinary examination of the relationships between gender, sexuality, space, and place. Focus on social investments in race, sexuality, gender, (dis)ability, and citizenship as spatial technologies of belonging and power. Emphasis on queer and critical gender studies approaches to the subfield of cultural geography. Credit will be granted for only one of GWST 429 or GEOG 429. [0-0-3]
Course Prequisite:  One of GWST 223, GWST 216, GEOG 358 and third-year standing.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  GEOG 429.

------------------ Course Code: STAT, Course Name: Statistics ------------------

Course: STAT
Course Section: 121
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Elementary Statistics
Course Description: Descriptive and inferential statistics, elementary probability, probability distributions, estimation of parameters, hypotheses testing, correlation, linear regression. Cannot provide credit towards a B.Sc. degree. Good for CA, CMA credit. Credit will be granted for only one of STAT 121, STAT 124, or STAT 230. [3-1-0]
Course Prequisite:  Foundations of Mathematics 11.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 124
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Business Statistics
Course Description: Introduction to surveys and simple sampling strategies; descriptive methods for one and two variables; frequency distributions; correlation and regression; descriptive methods for time series and index numbers; and probability and relationship to statistical inference. Good for CA, CMA credit. Credit will be granted for only one of STAT 121, STAT 124, or STAT 230. [3-1-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of Principles of Mathematics 11, Pre-Calculus 11, Foundations of Mathematics 12.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 230
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introductory Statistics
Course Description: Applied statistics for students with a first-year calculus background. Estimation and testing of hypotheses, problem formulation, models and basic methods in analysis of variance, linear regression, and non-parametrics. Descriptive statistics and probability are presented as a basis for such procedures. Credit will be granted for only one of STAT 121, STAT 124, or STAT 230. [3-1-0]
Course Prequisite:  One of MATH 101, MATH 142.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 303
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Introduction to Probability
Course Description: Basic notions of probability, random variables, expectation and conditional expectation and limit theorems. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  MATH 200.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency:  MATH 302.

Course: STAT
Course Section: 400
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Statistical Communication and Consulting
Course Description: Development of broad guidelines for a comprehensive approach to data analysis with a focus on communicating statistical ideas from planning experiments to the presentation of results. Topics include criteria for selection of suitable methodologies, data preparation, outlier detection, and exploratory data analysis. Credit will be granted for only one of DATA 500 or STAT 400 when the subject matter is of the same nature. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  DATA 311, and fourth-year standing in the Data Science major or honours program.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 401
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Probability and Statistical Inference
Course Description: Formal introduction to the theory of statistical modeling with a focus on distributions of data, likelihood based inference for learning unknown parameters, construction of confidence intervals and development of tests. Bayesian methods will be used to contrast standard statistical procedures. [3-1-0]
Course Prequisite:  All of STAT 230, STAT 303.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 403
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Stochastic Processes
Course Description: Random walks, Markov chains, Poisson processes, continuous time Markov chains, birth and death processes, exponential models, and applications of Markov chains. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  STAT 303.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 406
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Environmetrics
Course Description: Foundation of the use of statistical concepts and methods in environmental science and management. Scientific problem-solving using statistical methods. Integration of the formulation of objectives, study design, and quantitative methods appropriate for the design. The role and use of statistical software packages. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite:  STAT 230.
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Advanced Statistical Modelling
Course Description: Least-squares, generalized least-squares and likelihood estimation. Theory and application of parametric and non-parametric regression models such as splines, penalized splines, and generalized additive models. Assessment and treatment of data issues including missingness and measurement error. Credit will be granted for only one of DATA 410 or STAT 538. [3-2-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 547
Course Credits: 2-15
Course Title: Topics in Statistics
Course Description: Topics chosen from different areas within the field of statistics, such as time series, longitudinal and multi-level modelling, multivariate analysis, machine learning, resampling and permutation methods, smoothing and filtering, survival analysis, sports analytics and spatial statistics. Content will be determined so as to complement course offerings and meet the needs of the students. With the permission of the department head, this course may be taken more than once on a different topic. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite: None
Course Corequisite: None
Course Equivalency: None

Course: STAT
Course Section: 560
Course Credits: 3
Course Title: Probability and Stochastic Processes
Course Description: Theory of probability, including random variables, expectation, conditional expectation, generating functions, modes of convergence of random variables and their distributions. Applications to random models such as Markov, Poisson, birth-death, Gaussian and diffusion processes. [3-0-0]
Course Prequisite: None
